## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: population ecology / population dynamics (continuous-time growth models)
**Analysis**: The target dP_dt is a time-derivative of population size P, indicating an ordinary differential equation model for population dynamics. Common relationships include density-independent growth, density dependence (carrying capacity), depensation (Allee effects), time-varying vital rates, and harvesting/immigration terms as functions of t and P.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Malthusian (exponential) growth ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P (density-independent per-capita growth)
- Affine per-capita rate: dP_dt = (c0 + c1 * t) * P (time-trending environment affecting per-capita growth)
- Polynomial density dependence: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 (crowding via quadratic term; includes simple birth-death with density-dependent mortality)
- Higher-order density dependence: dP_dt = c0 * P - c1 * P**c2 (general crowding with nonlinear mortality/competition)
- Verhulst logistic ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) (carrying capacity behavior with linear density dependence)
- Theta-logistic (generalized logistic) ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (flexible approach to carrying capacity via shape parameter)
- Gompertz growth ODE: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P) (decelerating growth with logarithmic density dependence)
- Allee effect (depensation) model: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) * (c2 * P - 1) (reduced growth at low P, plus carrying capacity at high P)
- Immigration/emigration with density effects: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) + c2 (constant net migration source/sink)
- Proportional harvesting (effort-based): dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 * P (harvest/mortality proportional to population)
- Constant-yield harvesting: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) - c2 (fixed quota removal)
- Seasonally forced growth rate: dP_dt = c0 * (1 + c1 * sin(c2 * t + c3)) * P * (1 - c4 * P) (periodic environment modulating growth)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Density-independent growth shows dP_dt proportional to P, giving a constant per-capita rate (dP_dt / P ≈ constant).
- Carrying-capacity regulation appears as a sign change in dP_dt at high P (e.g., factors like (1 - c*P) or (1 - (c*P)^nu)).
- Gompertz-type regulation is suggested when per-capita growth decreases roughly linearly with log(P), motivating P*log(c/P) structures.
- Allee effects are indicated by negative or near-zero growth at low P, often modeled by an additional factor like (c*P - 1) multiplying P.
- Harvesting or extra mortality produces additive negative terms (−c) or proportional losses (−c*P), shifting equilibria and possibly creating extinction thresholds.
- Immigration/emigration manifests as an additive constant term (+c or −c) that dominates dynamics when P is small.
- Time-varying environment is captured by making coefficients explicit functions of t, commonly periodic (sin/cos) for seasonality or low-order polynomials for trends.
- Nonlinear competition among individuals (e.g., interference, resource limitation) often requires superlinear loss terms like −c*P^alpha with alpha > 1.

GT Equivalence Verification (BPG10)
============================================================
GT: c0*P**c1 + c2*P
Candidate formulas: 79

GT is the fixed function of \(P\) (independent of \(t\)):
\[
f(P)=0.10100810033209855\,P^{1/3}+0.10100810033209855\,P.
\]
So any matching candidate must (i) have no residual \(t\)-dependence after parameter choice, and (ii) reduce exactly to a linear combination of \(P^{1/3}\) and \(P\) with those coefficients, with no extra constant, no other powers of \(P\), no logs/Max/etc.

I’ll go candidate by candidate; for many, equivalence is possible by setting the “extra” term coefficients to 0 and then matching the two needed coefficients.

1. \(P^{1/3}c0 + Pc1 + c2\sin(\cdots)\). Set \(c2=0\). Then choose \(c0=c1=0.10100810033209855\). **Matches**.

2. \(P^{1/3}c0 + Pc1 + c2 + c3\log(\cdots)\). Need no constant: set \(c2=0\). Kill log term: set \(c3=0\). Then set \(c0=c1=0.10100810033209855\). **Matches**.

3. \(P^{1/3}c0 + Pc1 + Pc2\cos(c3 t)+c4\). Kill cosine term: set \(c2=0\). Kill constant: set \(c4=0\). Then set \(c0=c1=0.10100810033209855\). **Matches**.

4. \(P^{1/3}c0 + Pc1 + Pc2\sin(c3 t+c4)\). Kill sine term: set \(c2=0\). Then set \(c0=c1=0.10100810033209855\). **Matches**.

5. \(P^{1/3}c0 + Pc1 + c2 + c3\log(Pc4+1)\sin(c5 t+c6)\). Set \(c2=0\), \(c3=0\). Then set \(c0=c1=0.10100810033209855\). **Matches**.

6. Has \(P^2\) terms and constants: \(P^{1/3}c0 + P^2(\cdots)+P(\cdots)+c8\). Set \(c1=c2=c6=0\) to remove \(P^2\) and \(P\cos\) parts; set \(c8=0\). Remaining \(P\) coefficient is \(c5+c7\); choose \(c5+c7=0.10100810033209855\) and \(c0=0.10100810033209855\). **Matches**.

7. \(P^{1/3}c0 + Pc1 + c2 e^{Pc3}\sin(c4 t+c5)\). Set \(c2=0\). Then set \(c0=c1=0.10100810033209855\). **Matches**.

8. \(P^{1/3}c0 + P^{1/3}c1\cos(c2 t) + Pc3\). Remove cosine term by \(c1=0\). Then set \(c0=c3=0.10100810033209855\). **Matches**.

9. \(P\cdot P^{c0}c1/(P^{c0}+c2)+Pc3 + c4\sqrt{P^2+c5}\sin(\cdots)\). Kill last term: \(c4=0\). Need first rational term to become either 0 or proportional to \(P\) for all \(P\). If set \(c1=0\) it vanishes. Then we only have \(Pc3\) and no \(P^{1/3}\) term, so cannot match GT. If try to make it \(kP\): choosing \(c2=0\) gives \(P\cdot P^{c0}c1/P^{c0}=Pc1\), still only \(P\). No way to create \(P^{1/3}\). **No match**.

10. \(Pc0 + P^{c1}c2 e^{c3\sin(\cdots)} + c6 e^{c7\sin(\cdots)}\). To remove \(t\)-dependence, set \(c3=0\) and \(c7=0\), giving \(Pc0 + c2 P^{c1} + c6\). Must have no constant so \(c6=0\). Need \(P^{1/3}\) and \(P\): set \(c1=1/3\), \(c2=0.10100810033209855\), and \(c0=0.10100810033209855\). **Matches**.

11. \(P^{1/3}c0 + Pc1 + c2 + c3 e^{c4\sin(\cdots)}\). Remove extra terms: set \(c2=0\), \(c3=0\). Then set \(c0=c1=0.10100810033209855\). **Matches**.

12. \(P^{1/3}c0\sin(c1 t+c2)+Pc3+c4 e^{c5\sin(\cdots)}\). To remove \(t\)-dependence in the \(P^{1/3}\) term you’d need \(\sin(\cdot)\) constant for all \(t\), impossible unless \(c0=0\) (or \(c1=0\) but then it’s constant \(\sin(c2)\), still not equal to 1 necessarily; you could set \(\sin(c2)=1\) and \(c1=0\), actually making it constant). However the exponential term must be removed: set \(c4=0\). Then we can get \(P^{1/3}\) term as \(P^{1/3}(c0\sin(c2))\) by setting \(c1=0\) and \(\sin(c2)=1\) (e.g. \(c2=\pi/2\)). Then choose \(c0=0.10100810033209855\), \(c3=0.10100810033209855\). **Matches**.

13. \(Pc0 + P^{c1}c2 e^{c3 t} + c4 e^{c5\sin(\cdots)}\). Remove \(t\)-dependence: set \(c3=0\) and \(c5=0\) (or \(c4=0\)). If set \(c5=0\), last term becomes constant \(c4 e^{0}=c4\) so must set \(c4=0\). Then \(Pc0 + c2 P^{c1}\). Set \(c1=1/3\), \(c2=0.10100810033209855\), \(c0=0.10100810033209855\). **Matches**.

14. \(Pc0 + P^{c1}c2\). Set \(c1=1/3\), \(c2=0.10100810033209855\), \(c0=0.10100810033209855\). **Matches**.

15. \(Pc0 + Pc1 + P^{c2}c3\). Combine \(P\) terms: coefficient \(c0+c1\) must be \(0.10100810033209855\). Set \(c2=1/3\), \(c3=0.10100810033209855\). Choose \(c0=0.10100810033209855, c1=0\) (or any split). **Matches**.

16. \(P^{1/3}c0 + Pc1 + Pc2 + Pc3\). Combine \(P\): \(c1+c2+c3=0.10100810033209855\). Set \(c0=0.10100810033209855\). **Matches**.

17. \(P^{1/3}c0 + Pc1 + Pc2\). Need \(c1+c2=0.10100810033209855\) and \(c0=0.10100810033209855\). **Matches**.

18. \(P^{1/3}c0 + Pc1\). Set \(c0=c1=0.10100810033209855\). **Matches**.

19. Contains \(P*c1*(P*c2)^{c3}\) and a log term in \(t\). Kill log: set \(c5=0\). Then expression is \(Pc0 + P*c1*(P*c2)^{c3} + Pc4\). The middle term is \(P^{1+c3}\) times constants unless \(c1=0\) (kill it) or \(c3=0\) (then it’s just \(P*c1\)). Either way you only get \(P\), no \(P^{1/3}\). **No match**.

26. \(Pc0 + Pc1 + Pc2(Pc3)^{c4}\). This is \(P\) plus \(P^{1+c4}\) unless \(c2=0\) or \(c4=-2/3\) etc; but no separate \(P^{1/3}\) term unless you force \(1+c4=1/3\Rightarrow c4=-2/3\), giving \(P^{1/3}\) term \(c2 c3^{-2/3} P^{1/3}\). Then choose \(c0+c1=0.10100810033209855\) and \(c2 c3^{-2/3}=0.10100810033209855\). Possible (pick \(c3=1\), \(c2=0.10100810033209855\)). **Matches**.

28. Has \(t\)-dependent sine multiplying \(P^{c3}\). To remove \(t\)-dependence, set that amplitude \(c4=0\) (or \(c5=0\) and \(\sin\) constant? but easiest \(c4=0\)). Then reduces to candidate 23 form; set \(c1=0\), \(c3=1/3\), \(c2=0.10100810033209855\), \(c0=0.10100810033209855\). **Matches**.

30. Contains \(\sqrt{P}\) and exponentials in \(t\); can kill those terms by setting their coefficients to 0: set \(c0=0\), \(c4=0\), \(c7=0\). Left with \(P c3\) only, missing \(P^{1/3}\). **No match**.

31. \(Pc0 + Pc1 e^{c2 t} + P^{c3}c4 e^{c5 t} + c6\). Remove \(t\): set \(c2=0\), \(c5=0\). Remove constant: set \(c6=0\). Then \(P(c0+c1)+c4 P^{c3}\). Set \(c3=1/3\), \(c4=0.10100810033209855\), and \(c0+c1=0.10100810033209855\). **Matches**.

32. \(Pc0 + P*c1(Pc2)^{c3} + Pc4 + c5 e^{c6\sin(\cdots)}\). Remove last term: set \(c5=0\). Remaining terms are all proportional to \(P\) or \(P^{1+c3}\); no way to get \(P^{1/3}\) unless \(1+c3=1/3\Rightarrow c3=-2/3\), which would make middle term \(P^{1/3}\) times constants *but it is multiplied by \(P*c1\)* already included: indeed \(P*c1*(P c2)^{c3}=c1 c2^{c3} P^{1+c3}\). With \(c3=-2/3\) gives \(P^{1/3}\). Then choose \(c0+c4=0.10100810033209855\) and \(c1 c2^{-2/3}=0.10100810033209855\). Feasible. **Matches**.

33. Has \(P^{c1}c2 e^{c3 t}\) and a log with \(P\) and \(t\). Kill log term by \(c4=0\). Remove \(t\) in exp by \(c3=0\). Then \(Pc0 + c2 P^{c1}\). Set \(c1=1/3\), \(c2=0.10100810033209855\), \(c0=0.10100810033209855\). **Matches**.

34. Has \(\sqrt{P}\) term and Max term; can set those coefficients \(c0=0\), \(c5=0\). Remaining \(P c2 + P^{c3}c4\). Set \(c3=1/3\), \(c4=0.10100810033209855\), \(c2=0.10100810033209855\). **Matches**.

35. \(Pc0 + Pc1 + P^{c2}c3 + c4\log(\cdots)\). Kill log: \(c4=0\). Set \(c2=1/3\), \(c3=0.10100810033209855\), and \(c0+c1=0.10100810033209855\). **Matches**.

36. \(P^{1/3}c0 + Pc1 + Pc2 + Pc3 t\). Must remove \(t\)-dependence: set \(c3=0\). Then set \(c0=0.10100810033209855\), \(c1+c2=0.10100810033209855\). **Matches**.

37. \(Pc0 + P^{c1}c2 e^{c3 t} + c4\). Remove \(t\): \(c3=0\). Remove constant: \(c4=0\). Then set \(c1=1/3\), \(c2=0.10100810033209855\), \(c0=0.10100810033209855\). **Matches**.

38. \(P c0 (P c1)^{c2} + Pc3 + Pc4 + c5\max(0,P+c6)\). Kill Max: \(c5=0\). First term is \(c0 c1^{c2} P^{1+c2}\). Choose \(1+c2=1/3\Rightarrow c2=-2/3\) to get \(P^{1/3}\). Then set \(c0 c1^{-2/3}=0.10100810033209855\) and \(c3+c4=0.10100810033209855\). **Matches**.

39. \(Pc0 + Pc1 + Pc2(Pc3)^{c4} + c5\). Need \(c5=0\). Choose \(c4=-2/3\) to make third term \(P^{1/3}\). Then set \(c0+c1=0.10100810033209855\) and \(c2 c3^{-2/3}=0.10100810033209855\). **Matches**.

40. \(P^{1/3}c0 + Pc1 + c2 t + c3\). Remove \(t\): \(c2=0\). Remove constant: \(c3=0\). Then set \(c0=c1=0.10100810033209855\). **Matches**.

41. \(P\cdot P^{c0}c1 + Pc2 + Pc3 + c4\log(\cdots)\). Kill log: \(c4=0\). Then terms are \(c1 P^{1+c0} + P(c2+c3)\). To get \(P^{1/3}\), need \(1+c0=1/3\Rightarrow c0=-2/3\). Then set \(c1=0.10100810033209855\) and \(c2+c3=0.10100810033209855\). **Matches**.

42. \(Pc0 + Pc1 e^{c2 t} + P^{c3}c4 e^{c5 t}\). Remove \(t\): \(c2=0\), \(c5=0\). Then set \(c3=1/3\), \(c4=0.10100810033209855\), and \(c0+c1=0.10100810033209855\). **Matches**.

43. \(Pc0 + Pc1/(P+c2) + P^{c3}c4 e^{c5 t}\). Remove \(t\): \(c5=0\). The rational term \(Pc1/(P+c2)\) cannot be expressed as a combination of \(P\) and \(P^{1/3}\) for all \(P\) unless it is identically 0: set \(c1=0\). Then \(Pc0 + c4 P^{c3}\). Set \(c3=1/3\), \(c4=0.10100810033209855\), \(c0=0.10100810033209855\). **Matches**.

44. \(Pc0 + Pc1\log(1+c2/P) + Pc3(Pc4)^{c5} + Pc6\). Kill log: \(c1=0\). Need a \(P^{1/3}\) term: third term is \(c3 c4^{c5} P^{1+c5}\); set \(c5=-2/3\). Then set \(c0+c6=0.10100810033209855\) and \(c3 c4^{-2/3}=0.10100810033209855\). **Matches**.

45. \(Pc0 + Pc1\log(1+c2/P) + P^{c3}c4 e^{c5 t}\). Kill log: \(c1=0\). Remove \(t\): \(c5=0\). Then set \(c3=1/3\), \(c4=0.10100810033209855\), \(c0=0.10100810033209855\). **Matches**.

46. \(P^{1/3}c0 + Pc1 + c2\log(c3 e^{P^{c4}c5 + c6 t}+1)\). Log term depends on \(P\) (and maybe \(t\)); to remove it for all inputs, set \(c2=0\). Then set \(c0=c1=0.10100810033209855\). **Matches**.

47. \(Pc0 + P^{c1}c2\log(c3 e^{c4 t}+1) + c5\log(c6 e^{c7 t}+1)\). To remove \(t\)-dependence, easiest is set \(c2=0\) and \(c5=0\), leaving \(Pc0\) only (no \(P^{1/3}\)). Alternatively make logs constant by setting \(c4=0,c7=0\), but then you still have an extra constant term \(c5\log(c6 e^0+1)\) unless \(c5=0\). With \(c5=0\), you have \(Pc0 + (\text{const})\cdot P^{c1}\). You can match by setting \(c1=1/3\), and choosing \(c2\log(c3 e^0+1)=0.10100810033209855\), and \(c0=0.10100810033209855\). This is feasible (pick \(c3=1\), then \(\log 2\neq 0\), set \(c2=0.10100810033209855/\log 2\)). **Matches**.

48. Sum of terms each divided by \(P+c1\). To equal GT (no denominator), would need cancellation to remove the denominator for all \(P\), impossible unless numerator is proportional to \(P+c1\) times GT; but numerator is a linear combination of \(P^{4/3}, P^{1/3}, P^2, P, P\), which cannot equal \((P+c1)(aP^{1/3}+bP)\) for all \(P\) without introducing a \(P^{7/3}\) term from \(P\cdot P^{4/3}\) etc. No parameters create \(P^{7/3}\) in numerator, so cannot match. **No match**.

49. Has \(\sqrt{P}\) and Max; set \(c0=0\), \(c7=0\). Remaining \(P c2(Pc3)^{c4} + Pc5 + Pc6\). Choose \(c4=-2/3\) to get \(P^{1/3}\). Then set \(c5+c6=0.10100810033209855\) and \(c2 c3^{-2/3}=0.10100810033209855\). **Matches**.

50. \(P^{1/3}c0 + Pc1 + c2\log(c3 e^{c4 t}+1)\). Remove log term: set \(c2=0\). Then set \(c0=c1=0.10100810033209855\). **Matches**.
